O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, dear children, I have completed this book which is the assembly of medical knowledge and its explanations are complete through my statements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And in a vision I came to complete it with this treatment, which is part of the work of hands, that is "chirurgy." (Note: The translation here attempts to capture the essence based on an interpretation as direct translations from old languages may not always be literal due to linguistic evolution.)
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is fortified in our region and can be executed at any time, if there are advances made to this science as well as its codification into books, no delay remains for you on account of these minor descriptions found in ancient texts that have been worked by hands. (Note: This translation interprets the meaning within an Old French context where "uevre" refers metaphorically not only to physical dexterity but also possibly intellectual endeavor.)
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes mistake and pride, and intentions are closed off, leading to the exclusion of knowledge.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	And I seem to bring this assembly together following the path of exposure and statement, and gathering all forms of cautery tools along with other implements related thereto; thus assembling them for a skilled hand when it is time.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because none of our hands masters are found herein, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who enters into this should strive in the science of anatomy as Galen says, grasping the judgment of men and their forms and conjunctions and separations within them, along with knowledge of bones and nerves and sinews and joint count, movement that is moving or at rest, and leverage.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because of Ypocras who is with the sword and with the cautery, and in the art of medicine.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We say in the introduction of this book that anyone who is not conscious of what has been said before and avoids making errors, so as to help others understand their duties when dealing with this knowledge and its practical understanding.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	I see a madman who takes out abscess or the colon of a woman, and extracts her veins therefrom; so much blood comes forth that the woman is dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And to another view which betrays a joint of an old stone and the bone was large; he carried it away with him along his bladder, and died at court within three years.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have seen it happen, and the situation of the patient and the size of the joint were present; he was clearly in distress as they treated him with urgency.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And to another remedy that he took for our land, which had broken his leg and gotten an injury therein; the mires of ignorance forced the break apart at the wound as if by great force, leaving no salve in the place, until it came to its end. He ordered him not to detach anything from the wound; he stayed like that until the whole limb was swollen and returned to perdition.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I am called upon to come and help him take away his leg; and when I lay it down so that he can feel no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way of correction was confirmed for the limb, and it could not be healed therefrom; nor did the corruption cease to affect through any part of the lost member until completely gone.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And he who collapsed at the abscess increased it, then inflamed by its own malevolence.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Canker, when it is pure in black bile, requires only that we touch iron if there's no chance of curing what has become corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, handle children carefully, you must know that the art of hand is divided into two parts: it's about understanding excess in many cases; and I will show each lesson from this book where there are fear and risk.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	And so that they may be kept in check if children look at you with envy; take up your weapons as companions and perform the arts gently but firmly, using the best means according to God's grace—bring salvation and humility into this world; leave behind insufferable diseases for health; arm yourself so that doubts do not trouble you here in this realm with aspirations of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take any of your reminders for illness with you; do not call yourself foolishly blinded sight.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have applied this treatment according to the third chapter.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire and water caustics and the orders up to the joints; as well as shapes for springs/straps used in treatment, and tools necessary for this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, as well as compresses for wounds, arrow extraction, stones (potentially referring to splinter removal or treating injuries caused by arrows), and various necessary items; it also includes chapters on ordering the tools and shapes of springs/straps.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about the recovery of dislocations and sprains; and it orders what to do with the head joints of bones, and shapes of limbs.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus we remember the artwork; it is necessary for me to declare the quality of aid and potential harm from each condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and harm is longer speech and subtle science revealed through secrets returned by others who discuss these matters with us as we listen carefully to their words because I am concerned about preserving this knowledge for a long time.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that fire treatment assists everyone regardless of material; it is understood as beneficial for both hot and cold constitutions relative to the matter they are made from: essentially meaning its application suits those with warm dispositions when dealing with heat-inducing substances, and vice versa.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In warm and dry mixture of materials, none agreed and said that the fire cautery is great help; while another argued the contrary: that the fire cautery has no value in disease except for those caused by cold and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For fire is inherently hot and should not be treated with heat for cold diseases, nor by itself; yet those who argue the contrary say that the fire cautery provides great help in treating warm and dry illnesses brought on by men's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	When you purchase the skin of the body with its moisture associated with fire coloration, you cauterize the flesh.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For having found it never before through experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And with all means except for those fires only which he has experienced and knows through long use of the cautery chapter, and the variety in human conditions, and dispositions as well as causes of their illnesses, along with remedies and space needed due to tight timings; from others we never fear diseases cold and moist.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all their conditions gathered together agreed with the cautery. Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	The fire is simple, and it comes only to the part that is cooked, and does not harm any other member if poked.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The medicines that are hot arise from another member by withdrawing it; they bring diseases to the sickly part and do so due to their heat and nature unless there is excessive abundance of them.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees. Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know that these burns should be made at a certain temperature and with careful application.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that the use of fire cupping is permissible in all cases, because any harm resulting from its assistance occurs; and immediately it serves to alleviate necessary and urgent pains that cannot be endured by anyone except for greater malice not to enter into the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think that the sinew will not heal as others do; for a disease cured by fire cupping has no return; and thus it is now explained to you; but they are of little use compared to those who treat, because such measures only move the complexion and dry up the humors causing pain, and their worth lies in swift treatment and good management.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And when there is any choice in the disease according to the patient's complexion and their humors, they are gathered together within it if only excesses of food or moisture acquire them, just as with cauterizations for pain, and similar things, whereby thirst does not return; but this happens sometimes.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And not everyone heeds the call to apply treatments in medical practice; but it is visible that they do believe falsehoods and think that joint treatments are needed because when we administer care methods for any disease, these measures actually hold value once applied as a cauterization.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Open well then it is for healing instruments of medicine; not according to mere folk's understanding.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	They said that instruments of gold are more medicinal than iron and only speak about the quality of gold and its substance; they also stated that such tools do not cause putrefaction but in some men's cases I have found otherwise, discovering it is actually visible to certain individuals. They asserted that these golden cautery instruments hold greater value for mending than iron ones, as per their claims.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And whenever you heat the golden instrument, it is not when its gold color appears but after only briefly heating and cooling down instantly; if overheated at all, they will be burnt in this way; hence having enough restraint or limitation therein. Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use our fire cautery that has been worked out by our own hands.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	And if you have ordered this chapter about the joints' pressure points, so that the eyes can be found more easily.
dou cautere olivaire	By using an ointment (ointure) for a cautionary device
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	By moisture and cold in the head, this cautionary device is effective for diseases called "soda", which arise from various humors that loosen chief points on hair strands, ears, leading to countless dreams of depth and throat pain, commonly associated with illnesses stemming from cold.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patients are cleansed by medicine with healing properties, depending on what virtues and habits allow them to endure; then restore the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then he should sit between your hands, and place his hands on the back of yours; after that put the palm root up to the root of its nose between its two elbows; and when comes thy due time, if blood appears at once, douse with the cauterizing tool called "olivare", then it takes this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then he should place his hand under the sign of ink, and spread out your hands quickly while extracting them forcefully by tearing; afterwards lift up thy injured hand if thou sees a small bone visible to thee; and if not apparent, continue with the cauterizing tool until such time as said bone becomes evident; after taking four stitches of sinew or silk thread, place moistened woolen cloth underneath it, leave for three years; afterwards apply fresh linseed-soaked rawhide (burlap); and allow healing while the injury known as "tetrapharmacon" remains healthy.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they said that when more attention is given to the wound, it cleanses itself further, and if aid is provided for this reason so shall it happen.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these that one must much neglect the use of the cautery so as no part of the bone should break off, and then reset what has broken from the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they added that one must much neglect the use of cautery so as no part of the bone should break off, and then reset what has broken from the bone, and treat it furthermore. They stated that if a joint is displaced in such a way (bearing resemblance to an ovoid shape often used by women for their infusion vessels), one must apply force so as not to bruise the bone; after which, they stress leaving the wound open long enough to allow fluids to drain. Once this is done, it should be cleansed and dressed again.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of treatment are not suitable for all bones without exception; they were meant only if there is no fear in men or women alike; and movement seems necessary to me as the joints have become weakened by continued exposure, just like our other limbs show signs. Moreover, when a dislocation occurs within myself due to my nature (indicating that I am naturally prone), leaving it without treatment is not advisable - in fact, starting with more severe and immediate care suits me best; thus, I shall engage solely in the healing practices as recommended herein.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of anguish pain at the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When in the entire head comes chronic pain and lasts longingly, then should use the patients joint pills which are called "cochie", and drainage of chief and oils and plasters; and when they apply the fire cautery we have previously mentioned, and it proves effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	When the shoulder joint of a patient is severely ill and should not be too cold; then burn it with just as much fire as we have previously described above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After making the fire cupping with some horns upon the bone if as we have said before, and make I use glue for these small leeks; hold your hand so that you do not see into the bone: patients feel much greater pain in this treatment than others, and I will speak of it further; hence the fire cupping devices should be more subtle than those used to treat moisture at the head's joint, which is its form.
dou cautere dou chief	treatment for the bone (or joint)
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in one part of the shoulder comes pain alone and it extends to the arm, and there is swelling with disease as far as the joint; its dislocation spreads out through medicines purified by fire, and other cures I have described for divisions of diseases are done; yet none find relief: now I will make fire cuppings according to two methods, that is medicine made from water and fever.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cuppings of medicine from water if you begin with a decoction (alz), and peel off the bark and nutshells as for two dislocations, then apply it to the temple where pain holds in part; after they have been properly applied and left on for twelve hours or three, remove them and treat fever cuppings while leaving the wound until next two years or three; afterwards submerge cloth soaked in bear grease during dressing.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of cauterization while he is healthy; and if you see any other burning remedies that I have written or dealt with regarding burn treatments.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery, according to this method.

Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	Calls it "clos" because the head is made in a form of a clocket or has little curls and appears small; place this instrument by the painful spot with your hand held tightly over top until the patient's moisture ceases to burn, at which point loosen your grip slightly. Continue doing so until bleeding stops (here "keur" refers possibly to a type of wound or injury).
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After applying cotton with the sinew, and securing it to the joint for three nights; then apply finer wool dipped in bear grease, and continue treating this inflammation until healthy; when you cauterize this swelling using the "cultellare" lancet at its tip, ensuring not to cover the artery present here which is ancient.
de emigraine	of the inflammation
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraine as we have described in divisions of diseases, and gain nothing from it yet, then you must extinguish the medicine and iron tools before they become white; mark half a dozen paces along its length with your finger once, stretch out one hand without covering the artery, ensuring that neither bone nor nerve has any movement beyond resting. Also handle the jaw so it remains still when moved inwards, allowing only speech and spasm to cease for those who do not understand or are untested; let blood flow normally but be mindful of heavy fear and trembling affecting him directly involved with such ignorance. I will tell you how to staunch the bleeding once the artery is sealed, either by clotting or suturing, immediately attended to without delay for those who are unlearned in these procedures; but leave blood flow where it may within its course until then.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And when you see that these cauterizations do not soothe the disease and the patients are suffering, perform the incision here as we have said before, and treat the wound while it is clean; and if you observe further, administer one of the two cauters mentioned above or for arrow extraction with a knife-wielding cauterizer, which will be better than these.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	Of pain from cold in their ears
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes from the ear due to cold and we have applied remedies as discussed in this division, and the pain does not cease, then show forth this instrument called "points", which form is thusly described.

After puncturing the entire inside of the malady's ear, or where two ears hold their pain together, and you move upwards from the root of the ear until you find it with your needle; apply ten such points to each ear as cured while they are healthy.

de litargie	When treating pleurisy as we have said

de l’awe des eulz	From the hair of their limbs

de la cure de fistule par cautere	For abscess treatment by cautery:  
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat an abscess as we have described in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit, then you must make a cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to set their head in proper position; and bind down their chief with your hands so that it does not move or fall away; afterward apply a moistened linen or pomade from elder leaves on top of its oil (ointment); then heat up the cautery which is prepared thus: make sure it forms like a quill atop, assemble together the head using this instrument. Look and if one end appears to another's other end as feathers do to each other; or appear thinly spread outwards much like tent stakes would be used in tents - but all of these considerations are valued only when applied with your own methodology for treatment.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After the fistula opens up and draws out pus, then touch it dryly; when it is closed, if there's blood coming from the wound, cleanse with hot coals; place the heated cautery on top of where your hand rests above the oil to prevent erratic movements; put the cautery in the grease of the oil.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come at the beginning with fire cupping on bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you do not start with fire cupping on the bone, then repeat it once more if you know how to use it and leave it for three years; afterward place a dampened linen wick in bear grease as long as healing continues until sanitized over forty days. Then apply medicine that is corrosive by nature while the bone remains exposed, following what your chapter advises.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way to use fire cautery for an abscess which none of the elders said before.

et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit. Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the abscess is sound through the fire cautery we have described, it's beneficial (or good for health).

dou movement des dens	movement of joints

de la dolor des dens	of the pain of them (the joints)
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain comes from coldness or arrows (metaphor for injury), and the treatments of medicine are ineffective, then he has skill in two methods of cautery: charcoal cautery and fire cautery.

Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The fire assemblies used if it is such that you prepare a piece of iron or beechwood charcoal, and make sure the heated cautery does not burn in the mouth of the patient; after heating, shape it immediately for insertion into the tooth with your hand held until cooled down. And four kinds of internal grinding aids accompany each specific key instrument; and two such instruments for addressing chest issues, as well as two more aimed at treating groin problems using cautery techniques therewith associated.

de la cure des emorroydes	Of treatments for bleeding wounds
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés. Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre». de la dolor dou dos	of pain from behind
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, or through grinding down joints, percussion, excessive bleeding, or expansion of cold materials, none of these signs are enough reasons for cautery, except in those who come from a colder infusion.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	They should consider that the patient is devoid of putrid pills or other similar signs, applied on their back, lower spine, or where pain holds for three lines high-numbered marks and one line in any additional marking; make this specific type of cautery called "points"; if seen afterward, perform III points or IV to the clavicle according to its form:

de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	Pain in the joints caused by moisture that expands on any limb's body, and when pain comes upon stepping, they call it "podagra" properly; and when it is due to cold and medicine treatments cannot heal them, then treatment with cautery according to this manner: make the joint interstices by means of caustics, and apply the olive-cauter accordingly.

When the pains come down in feet or shoulders, cauterize those portions and apply proper governance (likely a reference to care), along with medicinal treatments for relief.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you provide good management and purge humidity (likely meaning the removal of excess moisture), they shall be well under divine care (suggesting reliance on God's help for healing).
de la routure dou syfac	Of the shoulder dislocation
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the dislocation comes from grief and it is new again, if you find that when curing him, none shall escape until evening falls today; and let him use things to draw out his belly fluids, so that he expels them through his stomach. Then prepare and use this cauterism tool accordingly shaped by grief's effect on the dislocation.
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until they are white and shining.

Be cautious so as not that the splint does not slip during application nor burn your patient's skin, preventing additional harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And when you come to the bone with your cautioner, your preparations are of no value.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And that the cautioners for children should be subtle according to their age and also substantially larger for adults; after three years of treatment with burnt cauterization until healing is complete, followed by other ointments as long as healthy again, leaving it on its back for forty more years so that the wound will properly seal up. Also, they must ensure their trousers remain lax for a long time to prevent them from popping out when going into chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of ulcers by fire cautery

C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This means the fire cautery and hot water cautery respectively.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	The fire cautery is applied as a comb for curling hair until it pierces the nail like a pen from above; made of iron shaped to extend beyond all parts and with delicate margins, after heating everything on top of the nail, turns his hand thoroughly around the nail until redness appears at its base. Thereafter, make an amputation wax molded into tiny pieces using a seal, leaving it in place overnight; when morning comes, remove the clots and they will be rooted out like tree roots.

Then apply hot water tightly with your hand, pressing down as you turn until the edge of the sack burns through at the base; find a way for steam bypassing directly into this spot (wherever heat reaches). Allow them only one hour suffering from the burning touch of cold water once. After that, let it be so resolved and their nails will regrow naturally in all directions to its roots.

quant li artere est copee	When the arrow is cauterized. (Note: The provided text seems to continue

And if it occurs without any sign and he has no medicine present, then must put his finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and tightly bind until it is secured above the wound and the vein; do not move him but apply cold moisture often so that it remains mostly frozen while he continues to be bound. Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of treatments for large wounds.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have said in the first chapter of this treatment all about diseases that require fire cautery or hot medicines, and questions and causes as well as methods; and I shall proceed to discuss what is covered herein by means most suitable for it so that we may understand more effectively.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele. de la graisse des eulz	of the flesh of the limbs

The manner of this work is such that the patient positions their chief (head or tongue) in a healthy posture; and then takes linen cloths arranged into a circle according to how much external fat contains each part, placing it on top; pressing down alternately with one hand and the other until the external layer forms within the circular arrangement; making an incision at the moist spot where fats appear under skin without allowing the wound size exceed what has been caused by cutting incisions into stones. Then makes a leather pouch soaked from perspiration, slicing through it to create a wider cut as needed for drainage; and continues until all fat is removed (presumably implying draining or removal of excess fluid); then takes additional measures when external fats emerge during the process. This translation attempts to convey complex medical practices described in medieval times involving treatment with linen cloths, handling moisture-related swelling, wound management potentially associated with lithotomy (stone incision), and techniques for addressing persistent fat deposits or abscesses that may require drainage through a leather pouch. The translation remains faithful to the original Old French text's attempt at instructive medical guidance using materials readily available during medieval times, such as linen cloths instead of modern bandages or drains and traditional removal methods for obstructions (possibly stones) within body cavities like bladders or urethras.

The accident arises from wounds and fissures, as well as cautery and similar things; for when you begin an arrow, it has two feathers on the shaft so that they enter in pairs down to the right side of the headpiece, then is positioned above all parts of the arrowhead, with a cap holding at its broad end.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the figure of the paper returns as it should be according to what is necessary for treatment, that's good; if not, then use a razor and place it in the fissure, turning over the paper again, making two more cuts or on either side of where you have previously cut out (which determines how much bone has come apart from its sockets), after which adjust these new breaks to form angles as they should be similar to a letter without an "I", then set that piece back in place; and similarly align the two parts, ensuring their spacing is correct like strands of linen thread.

Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the tool cannot enter into its place because it has too hard nails on them, you must prepare the "adze", as here is their shape:

And then immediately the joint is united and not forced too far; but I apply it gently until they return into place as we have said: And at the end of treatment, instruct the patient to lie down with their back covered in darkness; prepare lean meats for them without moving the head left or right, according to its arrangement till noon; then take out this tool from within the room and blind it, so that they cannot see anything. Afterwards, put on the leather strap wherein lies our seventh day's work: And there is not need now for you to perform these tasks in the surgery or immediately after incision but rather he must have his wound dressed with this material; because as soon as moisture rises rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When the candle burns out before the seventh hour of daylight, unwind its wick; and when it is calm, lift your eyes slightly to place them above their sockets, ensuring no daylight remains visible for any more hours, remaining in that darkened house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then take his bed and dress him therein; and let none interfere in this matter.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And ten therein who among us was from Yerac, saying that in our country water once flowed everywhere as if by magic, but we have never seen any such thing ourselves, nor found it written anywhere in ancient books; and perhaps this is a new phenomenon. Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the forms of Almada, whereby such who do not know them will see. And be made properly from rainwater.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of this subtlety remain and the limbs in three angles wet with sweat.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh as for seed (or semen). In essence, these
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Never do they germinate or appear disjointed in kind, and therefore there are none that seem scorpions of flesh from the seed; nor if any have colored flint or bony hue. Essentially, these texts describe a method where joints should not be separated but remain intact like rainwater (presumably indicating natural moisture), with limbs at angles likely related to sweat secretion and body parts highlighted for their appearance in terms of coloration—possibly alluding to dietary or physiological aspects relevant during medieval times.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In those instances of these bones which are soft and not fractured, must you make the patient sit between your hands toward the sun; and breathe through his nostrils into those joints, applying heat to them so much that under the subtle agitation provided by one hand beneath the pillow's cushion, until he perceives all of it bone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains none of it that can be covered up; and you cannot endure anything at all without clothing or undergarment on your shoulders; then get dressed as required by the circumstances above, whether through shawl or cloak put on accordingly; and when instruments are malignant, hasten to cauterize until they stop bleeding and become bone throughout all joints. Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced; then you must first reset the dislocation by tying a thick rope around its neck, using your hands for grip leaving some space between them. And hold each end of the rope to oneself or others who are present, and while doing so manipulate it back into position until they appear in their natural place; this task is light on those who know how to perform it: keep one hand holding its head that comes out by way of neck alignment with your own hands. The other chief (hand) holds the mouth whereby when moving them after each other, utilize others present for assistance as required rope ends are held between fingers spaced apart; and continue until they return to their original place in line or sequence.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Make it so long as you know that the joint has been corrupted by moisture, then repair the sinew, drain off any blood and dry out the sinew in Egyptian emollient, and return it straightaway to its natural position; do this for three years or more until all remaining signs of decay from flesh are gone. Then use a waxed thread intermittently each year as long as he remains healthy, and if there is need for medicines, then apply them according to the prescription form required by such instruments meant for cleansing; this represents their method of preparation using oils or other concoctions applied with these tools.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	Be it of silver or tin, looking like an oil lamp above, and lead you as if with a waxed thread; when visible, make another coil close to secure the head for use while heating the oil or any liquid. de la char sor le neis	of flesh from the nail
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times at the shoulder joint a disease that is called "such", and grows and becomes large as long as it looks upon something; thus they must first address this issue promptly, ensuring bone strength throughout before applying the cautery or burning medicine; if delayed until it becomes large, hardened in color, with poor sensation: never touch iron for metal pins, since these are embedded components. Once applied, any treatment can be completed despite weak sense of feeling from patient and caretaker's perspective, when treating the bone itself using such means restraining this condition.

Therefore it must come to no man if one regards the fresh wound; and then bandages their two hands together until they are healed, applying them wherever there is fear on either side as well as when both have such concerns—scrubbing all parts of their body till healthy. des apostemes des levres	Of tongue piercings
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the mouth there come teeth at intervals like grains of rice sometimes, and lesser or greater in size; then you turn the teeth backward and divide each one with pincers, taking them out piece by piece; after making an incision for vitriol burning, until they are no longer bleeding; then use a sponge soaked in iodine thereafter to treat dry things as long as it is clean.
de la char des gencives	from the gums of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper. Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Never assembled at the root of teeth between gums, which are ugly and painful sores; and never black or yellow with plaque until corruption reaches the gum, making it smell bad—when you put yourself in hand-to-hand contact to examine these things carefully so they don't move while removed. And thus use charcoal (black) and greenstone as well as other pigments; keep using them until dry enough for removal; if the first attempt is successful, it’s beneficial—if not, repeat at dawn or on high daylight hours with everything re-examined: these are tools to remove tartar. Note that dentists use different methods (tools) than those used by hygienes cleaning between teeth which have various shapes as per their specific tasks; and prepare all of them for your treatment, according to the demonstration you observe from either professional’s toolkit—hygienist's tools differ in shape compared to dentists'.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	You must attend to your patient's tooth pain as much as you pull it out, for there is no excuse in doing so; because this matter requires immediate attention.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When the patient's teeth are causing them to pull with uncertainty regarding their sharpness.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the patient suffers from tooth pain and ensure that it is extracted carefully; thus preventing any departure of discomfort through this process which we have already deemed necessary for these souls' sake. Furthermore, once you are certain about a sharply impacted tooth (indicating impaction), use forceps or fine instruments delicately at the first and subsequent touches until it is well extracted; then firmly secure your dental tools within your body—your hands being essential in this task —and place the patient's teeth between them, ensuring that they do not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly with brace wires, and if it jumps around freely, take any of these instruments and gently move them along different parts selectively, just like you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if they are perceived and manipulated, then must you fill them with linen or leather stuffings, the layers will be soaked, and if handled gently by pincers, it should not break during stretching; and also ensure proper alignment over the tooth for dental work.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take care that you do not break it completely and leave a part intact; then review the patient by addressing greater pains at the root's base, first pain location.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care that you do not act in such a way as these ignorant surgeons who by their haste and bravery shatter the joint without fail; they bring nothing but what we ourselves have told of - bringing about severe illness at the root's base, or fracturing the bone which is already suffering. And when there are leaks (of blood), wash it with wine or sagebrush and linen; and after cleaning up any seepage occurs frequently—often due to lead being used for cautery —if needed, apply vitriolic salt again and then recut if the bone is sound. If not, continue with caution (cauterization).

Here is its form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and firmly holding for keeping the bone in place; then restore the lead of medicines appropriate to it, if there is any putrefaction within the bone, and if so small. Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	Whenever the tooth appears not in accordance with its natural shape, and it is unsightly, particularly in maidens who must seek out how dense it is at the root of the tooth, for neither can they have gold or silver work on it nor file it down: herein lies everything required by this instrument. Here refers to a dental tool necessary when dealing with an irregular and discolored tooth that cannot be treated with precious metals like gold or silver, suggesting filing instead. The reference likely points towards tools used for the removal of decay (neis), shaping metal wires made from hardened steel ("fer inde agut en som"), which could imply a primitive form of dental bracewire treatment often associated historically with medieval medicine practices aimed at correcting misaligned teeth or orthodontic issues.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the peasant's hand and foot for all of winter time because you do not move them elsewhere; if it seems possible to shape his nail with a single stroke as this one is shaped, then so be it. et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And so it is made like the iron used for nails; and when shaping his hands and feet all winter long if he does not move them while grinding stone by hand, then at last there will be no rough surface left on which to work with metal tools effectively; as a result, his jaw becomes overworked and bleeds from the tongue's tip, should one need to smooth out sharpness until it is even without causing damage. quant li dent lochent	When the head of the shoulder dislocates
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth is loose, either through percussion or tapping, and patients cannot press against it so that they do not hurt, you have treated them with restrictive medicines; if these need to be restrained by a gold wire because silver becomes greenish-gray and rusty over time but gold never corrodes, making sure the wire is neither too thick nor too thin according to the space between teeth; when you see gaps in the spaces of healthy teeth, take up your thread and bottle twice through those clean ones, then place them at the misaligned molars as many times as there are or more (one or several), continuing until they no longer move. Then restart covering where you began, adjusting your hand subtly while extracting gently until movement ceases; provided that patients can not escape from their tooth roots if treated this way at the root of a loose tooth.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Cut the ends of the wire with needles and join them together; place it between healthy teeth as far as he can hold without biting his tongue down; leave it so thin that even if he moves or another thread extends out, until it wears out completely serving its entire tension at once. This forms the shape and figure of properly adjusted remaining two teeth and molars.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth loosens back into its socket piece by piece; as we have mentioned before; and no one interferes who isn't gentle or patient, making not a false bite of ivory denture, but places it where there is a gap, applying pressure like we described earlier until completely worn out. This serves the tooth in place for its entire tension at once.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of their tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No joints come from the tongue or nature that comes thusly herein nowhere nor through an accidental wound healed by your actions alone; rather this work is such that you must open the mouth of the patient and position their head, extending the tongue to its socket, then severing the nerve along as long as the tongue deviates from its place, cutting where there's hardness or bone protrusion—this constitutes a fracture; ensure not to overextend it past these areas for the artery present. After this is done with water-rose and cooler infused into lin cloth: change the patient’s tongue each night until no further suturing can be performed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And when the blood comes during dislocation removal, it is poured out from beneath the blade of vitriol; and if you find that flesh has withered away therefrom, then burn this place carefully using lentigo cauterization, which benefits those who apply it; afterward treat further until healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you see it colored black or dark, if the patient does not feel pain, do not touch anything at all, for it is gangrene; and if declining to a bleeding place with moisture present, pour some wine inside through a thin spatulate, delivering from both sides until heated enough, then return back into this work as long as you treat further; afterwards lift up the limb above and below, and cure other cures so that it becomes healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the throat slivers (Note: This translation assumes "apostèmes

Often comes from the throat with sharp points called "godath," and they are extracted precisely using two nails; when you treat them as we have mentioned in section division, if not healthy, take care: do not touch anything made of iron for these small hard stones. Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument here, then the form is like a pair of pincers (nails).

And one for pulling and the other as a name; when you have clamped down on one of them (the needle or pin), then hold it in such manner using this form which is like pincers, after making an incision rinse out the throat with hot, sharp cold water alternately until bleeding ceases from there—if rinsing does soothes any irritation; otherwise use boiled pomegranate seeds or thyme leaves (or mint combs), and similar things as long as it's cleaned. Then continue the treatment while in good health, but do not allow new pincers to enter there than just these two clamps accordingly arranged for griping.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And as a physician, I treated a woman with an abscess that was in her throat, known as the small sensation; and she had tightly closed down her entire throat, so that she could not exhale through the obstructed passageway, nor eat nor drink, and if she stayed like this for one or two days, she would die.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was as high up that I had to insert two drains by means of a nasopharynseal approach through both nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And at once I inserted an onion into one nostril and then blew through the pipe (presumably for irrigation), drawing out large amounts of blood before refilling it in from another nostril, inserting my finger to open her mouth and press down with a tongue depressor; thereafter I placed the onion back inside these passages. Only a small amount of blood came forth again until he grew bigger than usual—and then I forcefully engaged him (the abscess) within those nose channels: after which, no more bleeding occurred from that point forward as if God himself took over; and subsequently leaving only the remnants behind in these parts.
de l’uve	of the vein
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».
