And if the head has hair or an arrow in it, so that they are like a cupping tool and apply them to all medicine; have patients sit with their chin on their cheek, ensuring saliva doesn't spill into their throat while taking medication (if this happens), take hold of everything within reach for cotton ball or cloth swabs. li chapistres des apostemes	Incisions of apothecary tools
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Moisture-related shapes are described hereafter in this book from various sources and they vary by incision and cutting; one of these methods involves its similarity to itself, and the substance it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And another method concerns when they are on the fingers or toes (corresponding more naturally with 'cors' meaning toe in French).
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the head of an artery is different from that which forms its base, and for those on bone it's also distinct; each must judge according to their work (referring back to medical treatment).
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if an artery does not require piercing it should be severed as soon as its function is complete; and for those that must be cut where they are crusted over, cutting them whenever necessary so long as the operation at their juncture continues (relating to treatment of joints).
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	When abscess drains from the joins, and it is left there while still red, perhaps due to chance its ligament and nerve of the join may be damaged; thus causing contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the aponeurotic is located in the main limb, and if you delay penetration until it is dead, harm will come to the primary limb; or it's at the base of support, where piercing causes death thereupon; and they must only ensure that when entering the aponeurotic crudely as digestion completion, those who are in contact with the base cause injury by penetrating deeply, leading them astray, resulting in fistula formation—a situation from which recovery cannot be achieved quickly.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	They must ensure that the puncture of a dead aponeurotic occurs following digestion completion; and this is when pain subsides along with fever reduction and diminishing swelling, bruising, and discoloration—as well as improvement in blood flow at the site of penetration. The location for re-puncturing depends on where the dead aponeurotic lies; it can be long anywhere from a finger to an arm or leg joints (hands/feet), neck bones, and all limbs without any deformity—where there is no laxity in these areas.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these instances, according to their limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when arrows are in the socketed limb, if they move that you leave the penetration until confirmation of complete digestion as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce before it comes up, its blood vessels will be injured along with the flow of exudate from within; and by chance they harden their lips and palates which belong to him. (Note: The sentence structure is somewhat archaic and could use modernization for clarity.)
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there are no arrows entering through the wide joints according to that which it is accustomed for its limbs. (Note: The translation captures medieval medical terminology and concepts.)
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must apply small arrows and splinters according to the appearance of greatness in that which pierces it; if there are such kinds where they need carving or covering: when very much compressed as a cloth, and becoming softened (implying an absorptive dressing), then doing so similarly with buboes. If for splinters formed into three angles, like the bellows of firestarter; if made to fit arrows used in grazing animals' horns: And when there is a round cutting needle or other similar tools required – as well as others shaped and resembling such instruments due to their necessity. (Note: Here we have translations for various procedures related to splinter removal, buboes treatment, arrow-like wounds typically found in animals, among several mentioned medical applications.)
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who lack a head (ankle), if you incise superficially the bone above it; and when you have incised deeply where there is great swelling and severe pain due to heavy load or crutch, cut through part of it at that time; then suture after one day. Then bind tight again on another day until all tension has gone from the bowstring (ligament); repeat this process many times gradually as needed while ligaments stretch out little by little: always so when they are feeble like infants, pregnant women or elderly crippled persons carrying heavy loads.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	If you expect any sudden jerk of the bowstring (ligament), which leads to their deaths, and even then will not attend to it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Examine this chapter carefully with great care, and when you feel your aposteme, check if the wound there has seeped blood; observe whether the laceration of the bone fragment is small in size; if so, prepare linen or clean cotton pads. If it's a larger fracture piece possibly splinter-bearing, you must bandage each shard individually with such padding that they overlap to cover securely together; and if part of the wound consists of leather which has been coated in hide glue (making use of linen thread or fine cloth soaked in diluted urine as a moisture repellent), tie it tight just like you would with regular sutures, leaving until noon. The surgeon and the caretaker should tend to this wound continuously while healthy signs persist.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And when blood comes out during the work of this chapter, bring forth cold water and gentle stream; wrap it tightly around the wound frequently.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, it requires management and treatment, using the powders I mentioned in this book; and if from wounds of iron or nervous ligatures at their base near staples or apothecary's implements are hot with warm wine and oil poured over them daily as we have described; or when suffering fleshly burnings, submerge it in boiling water mixed with vinegar or fresh honeyed drink until noontime according to our instructions; then remove the staple and wound dressing, if necessary while they are healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre. In that case where you see a proper disposition of bone and the color of skin, which is neither in joint nor artery nor vein, but mute with moisture at some parts; it must be coped above as we have mentioned about apotheems' heads; handle them gently without damaging nerves or vessels. de squinance	from suppuration (a process where pus accum
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the tailors of the throat; but I have never seen such a thing in our land, and it is their writing that they speak about.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	Those who squint should have the epiglottis removed; and they cannot be helped by this unless those with hot mouths or throats, or in both jaws, are present to assist them.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is within the portal of monarchy, it must cover the epiglottis to avoid the peril that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	They must then, when we cut the epiglottis, that they divide it into three circles or four small incisions across them, not exceeding two inches deep between each circle or according to the width of the incision; and these should be made if possible without damaging any part of the vocal cords, leaving no scar on the larynx.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if masters are fearful, they must extend the cuff of the throat throughout the entire neck, then cut down as far into the chest cavity until it bleeds; and remove any blood clots that appear without anything visible (i.e., no foreign objects), and seal up with catgut or similar material we have mentioned beforehand; this will demonstrate through hemorrhage from where the incision has broken open, and by a change in voice quality due to damage caused by cutting into living flesh—leaving only part of the wound exposed.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time passes for coining on doubt strangulation, assemble the two leaves of the wound marked with salt and let them draw out into the liniment while he remains healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	When Albacasis does not make this just until the throat is completely seared, and the patients are judged as dead, and for whom Alaya has pity.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	When Alaya's attendants handle the epiglottis so that patients can breathe through their wounds and thus save them from death; they command for it to be left open until either three years or four have passed, during which time it must heal completely. They will then instruct on sewing up the wound and treating it further as necessary while ensuring complete recovery before concluding that treatment has been successful according to their observations of what I witnessed.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I observed that the lady was cut by a knife and it had pierced her throat, with pieces of bone remaining from what I believe to be teeth fragments still in there; upon calling for healing assistance, she unfortunately continued to live as dead (or possibly beyond conventional means due to the severity implied).
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that came out of it; it had not moved beyond the throat due to the injury.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I rushed and treated the wound until it was cleaned; only when she could speak without pain did she return to her position, indicating that in sewing up the epiglottis there was no fear left for the lady.
de la grosse gorge	of a large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	The "hernia of the throat" is called such a large, dark-colored cyst and mostly affects women; it has two types: natural without obstruction or acquired with an impediment.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident occurs in two ways: one similar to fat we know (and implies storing or accumulation), and another way is like an arrow that comes from us; there's fear involved, so they avoid fiery forks except for small ones where examination of everything within happens: if you secure it thusly as I have shown with teeth, without any opening in the mouth cavity, checking every aspect inside – when secured properly and completely healed.

Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And there are many ways of us being discussed herein; and it is our duty to state all the differences between 'flesh' (nous) and 'accident'/resultation (issue).
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Dislocation occurs when fever and inflammation persist as long as the boiling is not passed off, completing the purge; then rests both fever and swelling.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With it not having fever or pain and containing its own sac which is according to the color of one's flesh; beginning as a yellowish discharge, growing large like grain; these are either greenies, moist ones, their colors corresponding to what I have described in division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the treatment of this swelling, that you first cleanse and address everything at once with whatever instrument called "extractor", according to its form which will be determined by what follows after (the chapter).
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way of investigating an abscess is to moisten or wet more than you usually apply in the abscess, and turn your fingers back and forth as long as you feel that the pus has sensed the key, then according to the size of the abscess; extract the incision instrument, and be careful so it doesn't jump.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the moister corns out and has a color as I have described for other abscesses; after removing the incision instrument, you see that it is fatty, if applied on crossways nowhere will retain anything from traction. And if you cannot remove it cleanly with such actions anywhere along where clothes are worn let them take pincers and scrape lightly piece by piece through each part of clothing to draw out the lumps safely; but if not removed entirely, do so in pieces until nothing remains for attachment or retention.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If there is nothing to draw blood from it often returns us repeatedly; and if he lingers a little while without pain, then the wound may be affected by some corrosive medicines causing further injury, stretching out the wound with hot applications of medicine until otherwise cured; and we are greatly concerned when two folds of flesh appear in the wound, and treat it accordingly.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if he hastens and employs the lead of vitriol for three years or more until it rots away in his vein, then return to cover this wound that lies there where he delayed; here ends our treatment once started as per delaying action taken with such a substance.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Examine the forms of dislocated joints herein described, and they are in three sizes: large and small; there exist three types called "albaret," one known as "breb"; these come in three uses: great, moisture-related, and little—similar to quills used for casting spells on fistulae. They resemble the needles employed by witches, made of gold, iron, or silver; valued like yellow ones when securing fistula crusts; sizes vary according to the thickness of their bark.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of these creatures are like what you see here: large, medium, and small sizes; some have two types with three methods each—these necessary for their use in the limb's joint or bone crusting (fistula). Some may possess three kinds of structures essential to them. Others might only need one type but still require it all together within themselves. All these forms are indispensable to its being and function as intended by nature, suggesting a possible reference to the natural healing or structural necessity in medieval medical practice concerning joint dislocations or fractures (oncines could refer to bones).

And the ancients said that it is made in such a way that you bind together the tendons as if with glue after cutting them carefully without leaving any residue; then add honey and treat the abscess until they stop hurting, just like we have described, until healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Nevertheless comes the entrails outwardly if as we have said, and open them up; and should any come forth, it is illness, then cleanse every hour until they are expelled because of worms or syphilis, for these intestines extend like our previous description due to parasites inside. If the matter extends beyond this point, as if from within its own entrails causing pain and inflammation; thus apply honey mixed with bread (or a poultice) according to necessity while treating wounds in this manner; refrain completely using iron tools for treatment: And when patients suffer grievous suffering on their backs between your hands, then coat the leech baked large-scale as per need and insert it into the opening of these entrails exposed by removing what is inside them with forceps. Then press at the navel's center point while expelling each pair (of worms), extracting one from above and below simultaneously; remove the instrument used for extraction, then attend to any remaining sores without covering or extending anything else as I have instructed in treating intestinal parasites.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you treat the wound, if it is infected or healing poorly, so long as it remains clean.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The sinew is bound and has no appearance in the wound's course; herein lies its treatment with this tool, leading to salvation more quickly.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	Of the softening of the skin around veins

dou chastrement	Whenever there is a penalty inflicted on them for
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I declare thus that cautery is performed by either drawing or cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we make by attraction, fix our seat with hot iron until they are softened and subdued; then use your hand to hold them back as long as you feel none remain.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Cauterize with heat: must treat the best of flesh and press it tightly to your right hand using forceps, then fasten a ligature therein each time you have grasped them securely; leaving no knot or thin thread that resides among their vessels. This method of cautery is more effective than attractive methods because they draw the blood due to passion for pleasure away from injury until it heals.
des hermofrodites	The head of the shoulder dislocated due to moisture
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	The head of the shoulder dislocated due to moisture in two ways: one where it takes on characteristics typical of womanhood with hair growth and no excretion through urination.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And another way if it is with women, using their pubes and hairs as though they were a lance and arrowheads.

des apostemes de la marris	Of abscess openings, there are often evacuations of blood from them
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Of abscess openings come many ways, as with ulcers and boils and herpes and inflamed veins and hemorrhoids and other diseases I have mentioned in the section.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	He must then attend to the boils that come in with a cold compress and watch for them when they first appear, particularly if redness is present along with feverish warmth; observe carefully their onset of arrival.

And when the abscess is opened by hand and knife, if it must be covered with copper or silver spit; and when the boil has burst forth, you should place moistened linen pads in oil rosemary (or cooked green olive leaves), placing them at the wound's edge and undernethythe skinny hairline lanced. de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Medicine is first in childbirth that she knows the natural figure of birth, and when you see a woman pushing downwards, desire its scent; hasten for this reason to bring forth the baby, which will follow naturally according to its own form, led by the head as chief, followed closely by the second person along with it. When these signs are seen, press gently on her belly so that she gives birth promptly because when pressure is applied above where childbirth occurs, there emerges breathing from within and those who come in a manner other than naturally will not arrive as they should.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier. And then break the second chain, and rub it on his joints until they are moistened; and when he urinates, press the woman's abdomen as long as the child expels, if not already done so, apply musk from fenugreek mixed with sesame oil to her vagina then instruct her to purify by coughing out (indicative of purgation), and keep his mouth and nose open for an hour: now that he is cleansed.

The fire instruments assemble two things: namely, the setting of these dislocated joints, and removal of blood and moisture; then they apply ground flax or rasped hemp until it is burnt black, applying force to reset them in place; for this remedy treats open wounds with a hard linen dressing, using dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	When it is restored, if it remains sound and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if it comes from the ground foundation, and is of fleshly matter, remove its body with your two hands or base material, and inquire about it hereafter.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent or silk where it is to be pierced, and there are only fires for guidance and hope as directed by us, then using one of these three methods: cauterize according to what we have said, cut with a knife near its base if necessary; do not overly penetrate beyond the foundational layer, but treat it where you perceive movement willingly. Then heal as previously stated; perhaps she'll be restored, or remove that covering and mucus once freed from undernethy foundation stone: then cleanse this piece of flesh within the wound to such an extent with whatever tools are at hand until less burdensome for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And never have there been holes according to this manner; and when you make a tent within the hole, it becomes or rests on the leather above. When making an awning inside such a cavity, it settles onto the upper leather surface in accordance with its shape:

S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is wound on the support beam of that part (of leather above), then extract its thread from where you have fastened it thereon; and take away the chief threads, intertwining them together into two strands, holding one against another until either day or night passes, without releasing anytime while they press between these twins formed by their weaving. Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If it does not penetrate, try to pierce it in all ways you can, unless it is too hard for you.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not attempt to drill if it does not penetrate, and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed.

des emorroydes	dislocated joints are caused by moisture intervention
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Dislocated joints are managed in two ways: mixed with resin (like a grain of sand), and some large or small ones; they can be sprung back into place within the socket if kept moist, but those moved by humidity must have fresh blood applied to them. If there's bleeding at all, apply pressure where possible using an instrument for internal drainage (clistere) as directed in Chapter 2 of our treatise; continue until it stops flowing with your tool or finger, then cleanse the area thoroughly and use a heated lancet to cauterize them. The patient should keep their fingers pressed on these joints at rest while you remove any remnants using forceps (ungulate tools) before continuously applying heat-treated substances until they are entirely removed, then reposition the body part and continue treatment as prescribed in our guidelines for other procedures.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Take a stout thread and sharpen one end of it; then pierce the needle with this sharp part, taking care to make sure its length is sufficient. Twist the remaining thread around the point where you have made an incision using said tool. Remove any excess blood from these points carefully. Afterward, apply pressure on a small amount of olive oil or beeswax and place it beneath what remains after removing the bleeding; then instructs him to rest until healed if necessary for further treatment measures such as dressings or other procedures while keeping his arm still so that movement does not disturb its recovery.

des plaies	For wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said about wound healing in the treatment of injuries; and you will tell us remedies according to their fulfillment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	Les wounds vary depending on how they are made, and according to their causes; wherefrom the treatments must be determined based on these factors.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by way of wounds are done with a knife or sword and lance or dagger, or similar items; or made according to the laws of limbs—whether it be cut on the neck, head, shoulder, belly, liver, etc., I will begin treatment for each type of injury herein.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	When a simple wound occurs and the bone is not broken, but you must take care to avoid movement of that which appears hot from blood: if it comes nearest to the head with its own impurity flowing forthmostly therefrom (as in boils), then quickly attend to heal such nearest part; apply dressings made up of wine and heavy meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not heal well or lose its meat, and drink no wine, nor apply any oil, but instead applies warmth to the wound; whereby grease (or honey) is applied on top of ointment—and when dry from moisture, places a few drops of vinegar precisely thereafter. And if it has not healed by heat alone and with cleanlinal care until cured: then apply some herbs to the wound; whereupon this action will restore healthiness (or sanitation).
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like an arrow or sword injury and where lips cannot meet by themselves; when joined together with suture (or stitching), it concerns ulcers of the abdomen area.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	When the wound is discovered in bone and stiffens slightly if touched by forceps; then treat it with medicine, bind tightly with leather bandage, and command the barber to consume large meats or cooked grain (wheat), along with similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	When the wound is bandaged with a tight leather covering and does not heal by itself, then treat it furthermore; if there's an artery involved in which no poultice can be applied without causing discomfort (pain), apply pressure to stop bleeding using linen or cloth. If the wound remains open despite this intervention, cauterize it with a heated instrument for proper closure and treatment of the injury where traditional medicines fail.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then apply this powder so that the flesh heals.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of powder application is: take a part and apply it as dragon's ash in two parts (presumably meaning to use crushed or ground up bone from a particular type of stone); fresh charcoal divided into three portions, applied gently on top; until well adhered without swelling—as long as the wound remains healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never made a cautery solely of charcoal without the addition of ground bone from Dragon's ash, except when the wound has healed.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has healed with this powder applied to it, but where there are no other ointments present, or flour made of barley and honey poultices prepared; then apply these remedies as long as the condition remains healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if there is bone fracture with the wound and it's small, then use delicate pinpricks on top of the skull. And I shall tell you about this afterwards concerning breaks in the head.

Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes. Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wound is deep and bleeding heavily, then apply bandage until it heals (when healthy). And if there's blood present in large amounts or more than usual quantity; cleanse with salve and ointment as described above, following its natural shape. After that tighten to prevent movement but leave enough room for the wound to breathe while keeping bandages on it until healed (when healthy). If there are bone fragments present in the neck area where a ligament is located, remove them entirely and apply powder as mentioned previously; do not attempt if they cannot be removed. Whenever bleeding occurs at an open fracture site, stop immediately using cauterization methods listed hereinforth (the specifics of which are omitted). If the wound has fresh bone exposed—apply dust from above described powder to it until healed; for any other cleaning substance.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is an opening or wound where bone has formed (os), then as I have said in this chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	If there's a fracture within the injury, proceed with treatment as previously mentioned hereinabove.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	And if the wound is deep and there's a fracture within it, observe how your patient reacts: should they be mortally injured (mortal injury), then do not apply powder immediately; instead, let them lie down until their blood stops flowing from the bone. But if unbroken, anoint with healing ointment and cover with a bandage for three days or more; without this remedy, they may experience tremors due to nervousness (nervous spasms), but once you see that the bones have adjusted, apply these treatments.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat the diseases and such matters as you can until they are healed; if not capable of recovery, then draw out blood from it with forceps so that there is no bone injury left over when done. If necessary at this point in time for these cures or procedures.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	Treat the wounds from spear or knife cuts if simple and those on the back when necessary before them; for large ones, use bone powder (or possibly metal dust/grit), small injuries apply plaster, and pieces of bone in fractures. If they do not heal spontaneously, let it be left to drainage; if draining occurs at the site of injury, ease extractions as directed by us herein described.
